</td>
<td style="background: #FF952C; color:#000000; font-size:85%;">67.6<br />(19.8)
</td>
<td style="background: #FFC082; color:#000000; font-size:85%;">56.3<br />(13.5)
</td>
<td style="background: #FFE1C3; color:#000000; font-size:85%;">47.8<br />(8.8)
</td>
<td style="background: #FFF9F3; color:#000000; font-size:85%;">41.6<br />(5.3)
</td>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_of_Alabama" title="List of amphibians of Alabama">List of amphibians of Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Alabama" title="List of mammals of Alabama">List of mammals of Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_Alabama" title="List of reptiles of Alabama">List of reptiles of Alabama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Champion_Tree_Program" title="Alabama Champion Tree Program">Trees of Alabama</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg/220px-CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg/330px-CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg/440px-CahabaRiverNWR1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3282" data-file-height="2119" /></a><figcaption>A stand of <a href="/wiki/Hymenocallis_coronaria" title="Hymenocallis coronaria">Cahaba lilies</a> (<i>Hymenocallis coronaria</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/Cahaba_River" title="Cahaba River">Cahaba River</a>, within the <a href="/wiki/Cahaba_River_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Cahaba River National Wildlife Refuge">Cahaba River National Wildlife Refuge</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Alabama is home to a diverse array of <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a> in habitats that range from the Tennessee Valley, <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Plateau" title="Appalachian Plateau">Appalachian Plateau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ridge-and-Valley_Appalachians" title="Ridge-and-Valley Appalachians">Ridge-and-Valley Appalachians</a> of the north to the <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">Piedmont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canebrake_(region_of_Alabama)" title="Canebrake (region of Alabama)">Canebrake</a>, and Black Belt of the central region to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coastal_Plain" title="Gulf Coastal Plain">Gulf Coastal Plain</a> and beaches along the Gulf of Mexico in the south. The state is usually ranked among the top in nation for its range of overall <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-alawildlife_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alawildlife-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-outalawildlife_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalawildlife-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama is in the subtropical coniferous forest biome and once boasted huge expanses of pine forest, which still form the largest proportion of forests in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-alawildlife_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alawildlife-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> It currently ranks fifth in the nation for the diversity of its flora. It is home to nearly 4,000 <a href="/wiki/Pteridophyte" title="Pteridophyte">pteridophyte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spermatophyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Spermatophyte">spermatophyte</a> plant species.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Native_species" title="Native species">Indigenous</a> animal species in the state include 62 <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammal</a> <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-outalamam_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalamam-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> 93 reptile species,<sup id="cite_ref-outalarep_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalarep-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> 73 <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibian</a> species,<sup id="cite_ref-outalaamphi_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalaamphi-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> roughly 307 native <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_fish" title="Freshwater fish">freshwater fish</a> species,<sup id="cite_ref-alawildlife_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alawildlife-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and 420 bird species that spend at least part of their year within the state.<sup id="cite_ref-outalabird_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalabird-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Invertebrates include 97 <a href="/wiki/Crayfish" title="Crayfish">crayfish</a> species and 383 <a href="/wiki/Mollusk" class="mw-redirect" title="Mollusk">mollusk</a> species. 113 of these mollusk species have never been collected outside the state.<sup id="cite_ref-outalamollusk_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalamollusk-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-outalacray_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outalacray-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Alabama" title="Demographics of Alabama">Demographics of Alabama</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Alabama_population_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Alabama_population_map.png/220px-Alabama_population_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Alabama_population_map.png/330px-Alabama_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Alabama_population_map.png/440px-Alabama_population_map.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Alabama's population density, 2010</figcaption></figure>

font-weight: bold;"><div>Legend</div></div> <ul class="mw-collapsible-content" style="margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit; list-style: none; margin-left: 0;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1216972533">.mw-parser-output .col-begin{border-collapse:collapse;padding:0;color:inherit;width:100%;border:0;margin:0}.mw-parser-output .col-begin-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .col-break{vertical-align:top;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .col-break-2{width:50%}.mw-parser-output .col-break-3{width:33.3%}.mw-parser-output .col-break-4{width:25%}.mw-parser-output .col-break-5{width:20%}@media(max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .col-begin,.mw-parser-output .col-begin>tbody,.mw-parser-output .col-begin>tbody>tr,.mw-parser-output .col-begin>tbody>tr>td{display:block!important;width:100%!important}.mw-parser-output .col-break{padding-left:0!important}}</style><div> <table class="col-begin" role="presentation">  <tbody><tr> <td class="col-break col-break-2">  <b>Non-Hispanic White</b>  <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#dd7e6b; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;40–50%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cc4125; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;60–70%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#85200c; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;70–80%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#5b0f00; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;90%+</div>   </td> <td class="col-break col-break-2">  <b>Black or African American</b>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffe599; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;40–50%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffd966; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;50–60%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#bf9000; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;70–80%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#7f6000; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;80–90%</div>  &#32; </td></tr></tbody></table></div> </li></ul> </div></figcaption></figure>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_census" title="2020 United States census">2020 United States census</a> the population of Alabama was 5,024,279 on April 1, 2020, which represents an increase of 244,543 or 5.12%, since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_census" title="2010 United States census">2010 census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> This includes a natural increase since the last census of 121,054 (502,457 births minus 381,403 deaths) and an increase due to net migration of 104,991 into the state.<sup id="cite_ref-census_cum_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census_cum-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">Immigration</a> from outside the U.S. resulted in a net increase of 31,180 people, and migration within the country produced a net gain of 73,811 people.<sup id="cite_ref-census_cum_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census_cum-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The state had 108,000 foreign-born (2.4% of the state population), of which an estimated 22.2% were undocumented (24,000). The top countries of origin for immigrants were Mexico, China, India, Germany and <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Alabama is located in Chilton County, outside the town of <a href="/wiki/Jemison,_Alabama" title="Jemison, Alabama">Jemison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="United States Department of Housing and Urban Development">HUD</a>'s 2022 Annual Homeless Assessment Report, there were an estimated 3,752 <a href="/wiki/Homelessness_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="Homelessness in Alabama">homeless people in Alabama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Those citing "American" ancestry in Alabama are of overwhelmingly English extraction. Demographers estimate that a minimum of 20–23% of people in Alabama are of predominantly <a href="/wiki/English_American" class="mw-redirect" title="English American">English</a> ancestry and state that the figure is probably much higher. In the 1980 census 1,139,976 people in Alabama cited that they were of <a href="/wiki/English_American" class="mw-redirect" title="English American">English</a> ancestry out of a total state population of 2,824,719 making them 41% of the state at the time and the largest ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama has the 5th highest African American population among US states at 25.8% as of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>  In 2011, 46.6% of Alabama's population younger than age<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1 were minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The largest reported ancestry groups in Alabama are American (13.4%), <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish</a> (10.5%), <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">English</a> (10.2%), <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German</a> (7.9%), and <a href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_Americans" title="Scotch-Irish Americans">Scots-Irish</a> (2.5%) based on 2006–2008 Census data.<sup id="cite_ref-factfinder.census.gov_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factfinder.census.gov-145">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Scots-Irish were the largest non-English immigrant group from the British Isles before the American Revolution, and many settled in the South, later moving into the Deep South as it was developed.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1984, under the Davis–Strong Act, the state legislature established the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Indian_Affairs_Commission" title="Alabama Indian Affairs Commission">Alabama Indian Affairs Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aiac_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aiac-147">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Native American groups within the state had increasingly been demanding recognition as ethnic groups and seeking an end to discrimination. Given the long history of slavery and associated racial segregation, the Native American peoples, who have sometimes been of mixed race, have insisted on having their cultural identification respected. In the past, their self-identification was often overlooked as the state tried to impose a binary breakdown of society into white and black. The state has <a href="/wiki/State-recognized_tribes_in_the_United_States" title="State-recognized tribes in the United States">officially recognized</a> nine American Indian tribes in the state, descended mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Five_Civilized_Tribes" title="Five Civilized Tribes">Five Civilized Tribes</a> of the American Southeast. These are the following.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Poarch_Band_of_Creek_Indians" title="Poarch Band of Creek Indians">Poarch Band of Creek Indians</a> (who also have federal recognition)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MOWA_Band_of_Choctaw_Indians" title="MOWA Band of Choctaw Indians">MOWA Band of Choctaw Indians</a></li>
<li>Star Clan of Muscogee Creeks</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Echota_Cherokee_Tribe_of_Alabama" title="Echota Cherokee Tribe of Alabama">Echota Cherokee Tribe of Alabama</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cherokee_Tribe_of_Northeast_Alabama" title="Cherokee Tribe of Northeast Alabama">Cherokee Tribe of Northeast Alabama</a></li>
<li>Cher-O-Creek Intra Tribal Indians</li>
<li><i>Ma-Chis</i> Lower Creek Indian Tribe</li>
<li><i>Piqua</i> <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a> Tribe</li>
<li><i>Ani-Yun-Wiya</i> Nation</li></ul>
<p>The state government has promoted recognition of Native American contributions to the state, including the designation in 2000 for Columbus Day to be jointly celebrated as American Indian Heritage Day.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Language">Language</h3></div>
<p>Most Alabama residents (95.1% of those five and older) spoke only English at home in 2010, a minor decrease from 96.1% in 2000.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religion">Religion</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg/220px-Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg/330px-Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg/440px-Highlands_UMC_Birmingham_Dec_2012_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Highlands United Methodist Church in Birmingham, part of the Five Points South Historic District</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg/170px-Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg/255px-Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg/340px-Temple_B%27Nai_Sholom_Dec2009_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Temple_B%27nai_Sholom_(Huntsville,_Alabama)" title="Temple B&#39;nai Sholom (Huntsville, Alabama)">Temple B'Nai Sholom</a> in Huntsville, established in 1876. It is the oldest synagogue building in continuous use in the state.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg/170px-Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="240" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg/255px-Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg/340px-Islamic_Center_of_Tuscaloosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="960" /></a><figcaption>The Islamic Center of Tuscaloosa</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the 2008 <a href="/wiki/American_Religious_Identification_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="American Religious Identification Survey">American Religious Identification Survey</a>, 86% of Alabama respondents reported their religion as Christian, including 6% Catholic, with 11% as having no religion.<sup id="cite_ref-ARIS2008_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARIS2008-150">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The composition of other traditions is 0.5% Mormon, 0.5% Jewish, 0.5% Muslim, 0.5% Buddhist, and 0.5% Hindu.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information&#32;on Christianity in Alabama: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Baptists_in_Alabama" title="History of Baptists in Alabama">History of Baptists in Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Baptist_churches_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Baptist churches in Alabama">List of Baptist churches in Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Alabama" title="Episcopal Diocese of Alabama">Episcopal Diocese of Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_the_Central_Gulf_Coast" title="Episcopal Diocese of the Central Gulf Coast">Episcopal Diocese of the Central Gulf Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Mobile" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Mobile">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Mobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Birmingham_in_Alabama" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Birmingham in Alabama">Roman Catholic Diocese of Birmingham in Alabama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_in_Alabama" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Alabama">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Alabama</a></div>
<p>Alabama is located in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt" title="Bible Belt">Bible Belt</a>, a region of numerous <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> Christians. Alabama has been identified as one of the most religious states in the United States, with about 58% of the population attending church regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> A majority of people in the state identify as Evangelical Protestant. As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alabama&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the three largest denominational groups in Alabama are the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_United_Methodist_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="The United Methodist Church">The United Methodist Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nondenominational_Christianity" title="Nondenominational Christianity">non-denominational</a> Evangelical Protestant.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Alabama, the Southern Baptist Convention has the highest number of adherents with 1,380,121; this is followed by the United Methodist Church with 327,734 adherents, non-denominational Evangelical Protestant with 220,938 adherents, and the Catholic Church with 150,647 adherents. Many Baptist and Methodist congregations became established in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Awakening" title="Great Awakening">Great Awakening</a> of the early 19th century, when preachers proselytized across the South. The <a href="/wiki/Assemblies_of_God" title="Assemblies of God">Assemblies of God</a> had almost 60,000 members, the <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Christ" title="Churches of Christ">Churches of Christ</a> had nearly 120,000 members. The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian churches</a>, strongly associated with Scots-Irish immigrants of the 18th century and their descendants, had a combined membership around 75,000 (<a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_America" title="Presbyterian Church in America">PCA</a>—28,009 members in 108 congregations, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">PC(USA)</a>—26,247 members in 147 congregations,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Presbyterian_Church" title="Cumberland Presbyterian Church">Cumberland Presbyterian Church</a>—6,000 members in 59 congregations, the <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Presbyterian_Church_in_America" title="Cumberland Presbyterian Church in America">Cumberland Presbyterian Church in America</a>—5,000 members and fifty congregations plus the <a href="/wiki/Edgewater_Presbyterian_Church" title="Edgewater Presbyterian Church">EPC</a> and Associate Reformed Presbyterians with 230 members and nine congregations).<sup id="cite_ref-thearda_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thearda-156">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2007 survey, nearly 70% of respondents could name all four of the Christian <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospels</a>. Of those who indicated a religious preference, 59% said they possessed a "full understanding" of their faith and needed no further learning.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In a 2007 poll, 92% of Alabamians reported having at least some confidence in churches in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although in much smaller numbers, many other religious faiths are represented in the state as well, including Judaism, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalism" title="Unitarian Universalism">Unitarian Universalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thearda_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thearda-156">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jews have been present in what is now Alabama since 1763, during the colonial era of Mobile, when <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> immigrated from London.<sup id="cite_ref-shomayim_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shomayim-160">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The oldest Jewish congregation in the state is <a href="/wiki/Congregation_Sha%27arai_Shomayim_(Mobile,_Alabama)" title="Congregation Sha&#39;arai Shomayim (Mobile, Alabama)">Congregation Sha'arai Shomayim</a> in Mobile. It was formally recognized by the state legislature on January 25, 1844.<sup id="cite_ref-shomayim_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shomayim-160">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Later immigrants in the nineteenth and twentieth centuries tended to be <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a> from eastern Europe. Jewish denominations in the state include two <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Judaism" title="Conservative Judaism">Conservative</a>, ten <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">Reform</a>, and one <a href="/wiki/Humanistic_Judaism" title="Humanistic Judaism">Humanistic</a> synagogue.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Muslims have been increasing in Alabama, with 31 mosques built by 2011, many by African-American converts.<sup id="cite_ref-2011muslim_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011muslim-162">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several Hindu temples and cultural centers in the state have been founded by Indian immigrants and their descendants, the best-known being the Shri Swaminarayan Mandir in Birmingham, the Hindu Temple and Cultural Center of Birmingham in <a href="/wiki/Pelham,_Alabama" title="Pelham, Alabama">Pelham</a>, the Hindu Cultural Center of North Alabama in <a href="/wiki/Capshaw,_Alabama" title="Capshaw, Alabama">Capshaw</a>, and the Hindu Mandir and Cultural Center in Tuscaloosa.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are six <a href="/wiki/Dharma_centre" title="Dharma centre">Dharma centers</a> and organizations for <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> Buddhists.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Most monastic Buddhist temples are concentrated in southern Mobile County, near <a href="/wiki/Bayou_La_Batre,_Alabama" title="Bayou La Batre, Alabama">Bayou La Batre</a>. This area has attracted an <a href="/wiki/Indochina_refugee_crisis" title="Indochina refugee crisis">influx of refugees from Cambodia, Laos, and Vietnam</a> during the 1970s and thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The four temples within a ten-mile radius of Bayou La Batre, include Chua Chanh Giac, Wat Buddharaksa, and Wat Lao Phoutthavihan.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first community of adherents of the Baháʼí Faith in Alabama was founded in 1896 by Paul K. Dealy, who moved from Chicago to Fairhope. Baháʼí centers in Alabama exist in Birmingham, Huntsville, and <a href="/wiki/Florence,_Alabama" title="Florence, Alabama">Florence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Health">Health</h3></div>
<p>In 2018, life expectancy in Alabama was 75.1 years, below the national average of 78.7 years and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_life_expectancy" title="List of U.S. states and territories by life expectancy">third lowest life expectancy</a> in the country. Factors that can cause lower life expectancy are maternal mortality, suicide, and gun crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> study in 2008 showed that obesity in Alabama is a problem, with most counties having more than 29% of adults obese, except for ten which had a rate between 26% and 29%.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Residents of the state, along with those in five other states, were least likely in the nation to be physically active during leisure time.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Alabama, and the southeastern U.S. in general, has one of the highest incidences of adult onset <a href="/wiki/Type_2_diabetes" title="Type 2 diabetes">diabetes</a> in the country, exceeding 10% of adults.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Alabama" title="Economy of Alabama">Economy of Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alabama_locations_by_per_capita_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Alabama locations by per capita income">Alabama locations by per capita income</a></div>
<p>The state has invested in aerospace, education, health care, banking, and various heavy industries, including automobile manufacturing, mineral extraction, steel production and <a href="/wiki/Metal_fabrication" title="Metal fabrication">fabrication</a>. By 2006, crop and animal production in Alabama was valued at $1.5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion. In contrast to the primarily agricultural economy of the previous century, this was only about one percent of the state's gross domestic product. The number of private farms has declined at a steady rate since the 1960s, as land has been sold to developers, timber companies, and large farming conglomerates.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:RTJattheshoals.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/RTJattheshoals.jpg/220px-RTJattheshoals.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/RTJattheshoals.jpg/330px-RTJattheshoals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/RTJattheshoals.jpg/440px-RTJattheshoals.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="717" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Robert_Trent_Jones_Golf_Trail" title="Robert Trent Jones Golf Trail">Robert Trent Jones Golf Trail</a> has a large economic impact on the state.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Non-agricultural employment in 2008 was 121,800 in management occupations; 71,750 in business and financial operations; 36,790 in computer-related and mathematical occupation; 44,200 in architecture and engineering; 12,410 in life, physical, and social sciences; 32,260 in community and social services; 12,770 in legal occupations; 116,250 in education, training, and library services; 27,840 in art, design and media occupations; 121,110 in healthcare; 44,750 in fire fighting, law enforcement, and security; 154,040 in food preparation and serving; 76,650 in building and grounds cleaning and maintenance; 53,230 in personal care and services; 244,510 in sales; 338,760 in office and administration support; 20,510 in farming, fishing, and forestry; 120,155 in construction and mining, gas, and oil extraction; 106,280 in installation, maintenance, and repair; 224,110 in production; and 167,160 in transportation and material moving.<sup id="cite_ref-alaindustrial_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alaindustrial-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg/170px-Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg/255px-Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg/340px-Center_Court_of_the_Riverchase_Galleria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="399" data-file-height="599" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Riverchase_Galleria" title="Riverchase Galleria">Riverchase Galleria</a> in Hoover, one of the largest shopping centers in the southeast</figcaption></figure>
<p>According to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a>, the 2008 total <a href="/wiki/Gross_regional_domestic_product" title="Gross regional domestic product">gross state product</a> was $170<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion, or $29,411 per capita. Alabama's 2012 GDP increased 1.2% from the previous year. The single largest increase came in the area of information.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, per capita income for the state was $22,984.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The state's seasonally adjusted unemployment rate was 5.8% in April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> This compared to a nationwide seasonally adjusted rate of 5.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama has no minimum wage and in February 2016 passed legislation preventing municipalities from setting one. (A Birmingham city ordinance would have raised theirs to $10.10.)<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alabama&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Alabama has the sixth highest poverty rate among states in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, United Nations Special Rapporteur <a href="/wiki/Philip_Alston" title="Philip Alston">Philip Alston</a> toured parts of rural Alabama and observed environmental conditions he said were poorer than anywhere he had seen in the developed world.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Largest_employers">Largest employers</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Enterprise_lifted.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Enterprise_lifted.jpg/170px-Enterprise_lifted.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="214" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Enterprise_lifted.jpg/255px-Enterprise_lifted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Enterprise_lifted.jpg/340px-Enterprise_lifted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2384" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Enterprise" title="Space Shuttle Enterprise">Space Shuttle <i>Enterprise</i></a> being tested at Marshall Space Flight Center in 1978</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg/220px-Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg/330px-Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg/440px-Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama_Highsmith_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="554" /></a><figcaption>Hyundai Motor Manufacturing Alabama in Montgomery in 2010</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Shelbyhallcomputing.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Shelbyhallcomputing.JPG/220px-Shelbyhallcomputing.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Shelbyhallcomputing.JPG/330px-Shelbyhallcomputing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/Shelbyhallcomputing.JPG 2x" data-file-width="340" data-file-height="261" /></a><figcaption>Shelby Hall, School of Computing, at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Alabama" title="University of South Alabama">University of South Alabama</a> in Mobile</figcaption></figure>
