<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3></div>
<p>Alabama's agricultural outputs include poultry and <a href="/wiki/Egg_as_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Egg as food">eggs</a>, cattle, fish, plant nursery items, peanuts, cotton, grains such as <a href="/wiki/Corn_production_in_the_United_States" title="Corn production in the United States">corn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, vegetables, milk, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a>, and peaches. Although known as "<a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_and_territory_nicknames" title="List of U.S. state and territory nicknames">The Cotton State</a>", Alabama ranks between eighth and tenth in <a href="/wiki/Cotton_production_in_the_United_States" title="Cotton production in the United States">national cotton production</a>, according to various reports,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, Georgia and Mississippi comprising the top three.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Aquaculture">Aquaculture</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">Aquaculture</a> is a large part of the economy of Alabama.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-188">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Alabamians began to practice aquaculture in the early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-189">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> U.S. <a href="/wiki/Farm-raised_catfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Farm-raised catfish">farm-raised catfish</a> is the 8th most popular seafood product in America.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> By 2008, approximately 4,000 people in Alabama were employed by the catfish industry and Alabama produced 132 million pounds of catfish.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-188">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Alabama produced <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1154941027">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);clip-path:polygon(0px 0px,0px 0px,0px 0px);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">3</span></span> of the United States' farm-raised catfish.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The total 2020 sales of catfish raised in Alabama equaled $307&#160;million but by 2020 the total employment of Alabamians fell to 2,442.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From the early 2000s to 2020, the Alabamian catfish industry has declined from 250 farms and 4 processors to 66 farms and 2 processors.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_190-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Reasons for this decline include increased feed prices, catfish alternatives, <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>'s impact on restaurant sales, disease, and fish size.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_190-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industry">Industry</h3></div>
<p>Alabama's industrial outputs include iron and steel products (including cast-iron and steel pipe); paper, <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">lumber</a>, and wood products; mining (mostly coal); plastic products; cars and trucks; and <a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">apparel</a>. In addition, Alabama produces <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronic</a> products, mostly in the Huntsville area, the location of <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s George C. Marshall Space Flight Center and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Materiel_Command" title="United States Army Materiel Command">U.S. Army Materiel Command</a>, headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Redstone_Arsenal" title="Redstone Arsenal">Redstone Arsenal</a>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg/220px-Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg/330px-Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg/440px-Mercedes_Benz_US_International_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_U.S._International" title="Mercedes-Benz U.S. International">Mercedes-Benz U.S. International</a> in Tuscaloosa County was the first automotive facility to locate within the state.</figcaption></figure>
<p>A great deal of Alabama's economic growth since the 1990s has been due to the state's expanding automotive manufacturing industry. Located in the state are <a href="/wiki/Honda_Manufacturing_of_Alabama" title="Honda Manufacturing of Alabama">Honda Manufacturing of Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama" title="Hyundai Motor Manufacturing Alabama">Hyundai Motor Manufacturing Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_U.S._International" title="Mercedes-Benz U.S. International">Mercedes-Benz U.S. International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Manufacturing_Alabama" title="Toyota Motor Manufacturing Alabama">Toyota Motor Manufacturing Alabama</a>, as well as their various suppliers. Since 1993, the automobile industry has generated more than 67,800 new jobs in the state. Alabama currently ranks 4th in the nation for vehicle exports.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Automakers accounted for approximately a third of the industrial expansion in the state in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> The eight models produced at the state's auto factories totaled combined sales of 74,335 vehicles for 2012. The strongest model sales during this period were the <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Elantra" title="Hyundai Elantra">Hyundai Elantra</a> compact car, the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_GLS-Class" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedes-Benz GLS-Class">Mercedes-Benz GL-Class</a> sport utility vehicle and the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Ridgeline" title="Honda Ridgeline">Honda Ridgeline</a> sport utility truck.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg/220px-Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg/330px-Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg/440px-Airbus_Mobile_Engineering_Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2404" data-file-height="1500" /></a><figcaption>Airbus Mobile Engineering Center at the Brookley Aeroplex in Mobile</figcaption></figure>
<p>Steel producers <a href="/wiki/Outokumpu" title="Outokumpu">Outokumpu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nucor" title="Nucor">Nucor</a>, <a href="/wiki/SSAB" title="SSAB">SSAB</a>, <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Steel" title="U.S. Steel">U.S. Steel</a> have facilities in Alabama and employ more than 10,000 people. In May 2007, German steelmaker ThyssenKrupp selected <a href="/wiki/Calvert,_Alabama" title="Calvert, Alabama">Calvert</a> in Mobile County for a 4.65<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion combined <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_steel" title="Carbon steel">carbon steel</a> processing facility.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> ThyssenKrupp's stainless steel division, Inoxum, including the stainless portion of the Calvert plant, was sold to Finnish stainless steel company Outokumpu in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The remaining portion of the ThyssenKrupp plant had final bids submitted by <a href="/wiki/ArcelorMittal" title="ArcelorMittal">ArcelorMittal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Steel" title="Nippon Steel">Nippon Steel</a> for $1.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion in March 2013. <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Sider%C3%BArgica_Nacional" title="Companhia Siderúrgica Nacional">Companhia Siderúrgica Nacional</a> submitted a combined bid for the mill at Calvert, plus a majority stake in the ThyssenKrupp mill in Brazil, for $3.8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In July 2013, the plant was sold to ArcelorMittal and Nippon Steel.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hunt_Refining_Company" title="Hunt Refining Company">Hunt Refining Company</a>, a subsidiary of Hunt Consolidated, Inc., is based in Tuscaloosa and operates a refinery there. The company also operates terminals in Mobile, Melvin, and Moundville.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/JVC" title="JVC">JVC America, Inc.</a> operates an <a href="/wiki/Optical_disc" title="Optical disc">optical disc</a> replication and packaging plant in Tuscaloosa.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Goodyear Tire and Rubber Company">Goodyear Tire and Rubber Company</a> operates a large plant in Gadsden which employs about 1,400 people. It has been in operation since 1929.
</p><p>Construction of an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320 family</a> aircraft assembly plant in Mobile was formally announced by <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Brégier">Fabrice Brégier</a> from the Mobile Convention Center on July 2, 2012. The plans include a $600<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million factory at the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Aeroplex_at_Brookley" title="Mobile Aeroplex at Brookley">Brookley Aeroplex</a> for the assembly of the A319, A320 and A321 aircraft. Construction began in 2013, with plans for it to become operable by 2015 and produce up to 50 aircraft per year by 2017.b<sup id="cite_ref-apconfirm_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apconfirm-200">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcconfirm_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcconfirm-201">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The assembly plant is the company's first factory to be built within the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> It was announced on February 1, 2013, that Airbus had hired Alabama-based <a href="/wiki/Hoar_Construction" title="Hoar Construction">Hoar Construction</a> to oversee construction of the facility.<sup id="cite_ref-airbusasby_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airbusasby-203">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The factory officially opened on September 14, 2015, covering one million square feet on 53 acres of flat grassland.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tourism_and_entertainment">Tourism and entertainment</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Orange_Beach,_Alabama.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Orange_Beach%2C_Alabama.jpg/220px-Orange_Beach%2C_Alabama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Orange_Beach%2C_Alabama.jpg/330px-Orange_Beach%2C_Alabama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Orange_Beach%2C_Alabama.jpg/440px-Orange_Beach%2C_Alabama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>Alabama's beaches are one of the state's major tourist destinations.</figcaption></figure>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a>, Alabama ranked 14th in most popular states to visit in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> An estimated 26 million tourists visited the state in 2017 and spent $14.3&#160;billion, providing directly or indirectly 186,900 jobs in the state,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> which includes 362,000 International tourists spending $589&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The state is home to various attractions, natural features, parks and events that attract visitors from around the globe, notably the annual <a href="/wiki/Hangout_Music_Festival" title="Hangout Music Festival">Hangout Music Festival</a>, held on the public beaches of <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Shores,_Alabama" title="Gulf Shores, Alabama">Gulf Shores</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Shakespeare_Festival" title="Alabama Shakespeare Festival">Alabama Shakespeare Festival</a>, one of the ten largest <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_festival" title="Shakespeare festival">Shakespeare festivals</a> in the world;<sup id="cite_ref-encyclo_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclo-208">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Robert_Trent_Jones_Golf_Trail" title="Robert Trent Jones Golf Trail">Robert Trent Jones Golf Trail</a>, a collection of championship caliber golf courses distributed across the state; casinos such as <a href="/wiki/Victoryland" title="Victoryland">Victoryland</a>; amusement parks such as <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Splash_Adventure" class="mw-redirect" title="Alabama Splash Adventure">Alabama Splash Adventure</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Riverchase_Galleria" title="Riverchase Galleria">Riverchase Galleria</a>, one of the largest shopping centers in the southeast; <a href="/wiki/Guntersville_Lake" title="Guntersville Lake">Guntersville Lake</a>, voted the best lake in Alabama by <a href="/wiki/Southern_Living" title="Southern Living">Southern Living</a> Magazine readers;<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Alabama Museum of Natural History">Alabama Museum of Natural History</a>, the oldest museum in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg/170px-Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg/255px-Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg/340px-Mardi_Gras_Mobile_Order_of_Inca.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="599" /></a><figcaption>Mobile is the birthplace of Mardi Gras in the U.S.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Mobile is known for having the oldest organized <a href="/wiki/Mardi_Gras_in_Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mardi Gras in Mobile, Alabama">Mardi Gras</a> celebration in the United States, beginning in 1703.<sup id="cite_ref-MoMtime_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoMtime-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> It was also host to the first formally organized Mardi Gras parade in the U.S. in 1830, a tradition that continues to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-MoMtime_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoMtime-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Mardi Gras is an official state holiday in Mobile and Baldwin counties.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, Mobile's <a href="/wiki/Mardi_Gras_in_Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mardi Gras in Mobile, Alabama">Mardi Gras parade</a> was the state's top event, producing the most tourists with an attendance of 892,811. The top attraction was the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Space_%26_Rocket_Center" title="U.S. Space &amp; Rocket Center">U.S. Space &amp; Rocket Center</a> in Huntsville with an attendance of 849,981, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Zoo" title="Birmingham Zoo">Birmingham Zoo</a> with 543,090. Of the parks and natural destinations, Alabama's Gulf Coast topped the list with 6,700,000 visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama has historically been a popular region for film shoots due to its diverse landscapes and contrast of environments.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Movies filmed in Alabama include <i><a href="/wiki/Close_Encounters_of_the_Third_Kind" title="Close Encounters of the Third Kind">Close Encounters of the Third Kind</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Out" title="Get Out">Get Out</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/42_(film)" title="42 (film)">42</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Selma_(film)" title="Selma (film)">Selma</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Fish" title="Big Fish">Big Fish</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Final_Destination" title="The Final Destination">The Final Destination</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Due_Date" title="Due Date">Due Date</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Need_for_Speed_(film)" title="Need for Speed (film)">Need for Speed</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Healthcare">Healthcare</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/UAB_Hospital" title="UAB Hospital">UAB Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Alabama" title="University of South Alabama">USA Health University Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntsville_Hospital_System" title="Huntsville Hospital System">Huntsville Hospital</a>, and Children's Hospital of Alabama are the only <a href="/wiki/Trauma_center" title="Trauma center">Level<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>I trauma centers</a> in Alabama.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> UAB is the largest state government employer in Alabama, with a workforce of about 18,000.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> A 2017 study found that Alabama had the least competitive health insurance market in the country, with <a href="/wiki/Blue_Cross_and_Blue_Shield_of_Alabama" title="Blue Cross and Blue Shield of Alabama">Blue Cross and Blue Shield of Alabama</a> having a market share of 84% followed by <a href="/wiki/UnitedHealth_Group" title="UnitedHealth Group">UnitedHealth Group</a> at 7%.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Banking">Banking</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg/220px-Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg/330px-Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg/440px-Birmingham_skyscrapers_Nov_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Regions-Harbert_Plaza" title="Regions-Harbert Plaza">Regions-Harbert Plaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regions_Center_(Birmingham)" title="Regions Center (Birmingham)">Regions Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Tower_(Birmingham)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wells Fargo Tower (Birmingham)">Wells Fargo Tower</a> in Birmingham's financial district</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Regions_Financial_Corporation" title="Regions Financial Corporation">Regions Financial Corporation</a> is the largest bank headquartered in or operating in Alabama. <a href="/wiki/PNC_Financial_Services" title="PNC Financial Services">PNC Financial Services</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> also have a major presence in Alabama.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> has a regional headquarters, an operations center campus, and a $400<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million data center in Birmingham. Many smaller banks are also headquartered in the Birmingham area, including ServisFirst and New South Federal Savings Bank. Birmingham also serves as the headquarters for several large investment management companies, including <a href="/wiki/Harbert_Management_Corporation" title="Harbert Management Corporation">Harbert Management Corporation</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Electronics_and_communications">Electronics and communications</h3></div>
<p>Telecommunications provider <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a>, has a major presence in Alabama with several large offices in Birmingham.
</p><p>Many technology companies are headquartered in Huntsville, such as <a href="/wiki/ADTRAN" class="mw-redirect" title="ADTRAN">ADTRAN</a>, a network access company; <a href="/wiki/Intergraph" title="Intergraph">Intergraph</a>, a computer graphics company; and <a href="/wiki/Avocent" title="Avocent">Avocent</a>, an IT infrastructure company.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Construction">Construction</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brasfield_%26_Gorrie" title="Brasfield &amp; Gorrie">Brasfield &amp; Gorrie</a>, <a href="/wiki/BE%26K" title="BE&amp;K">BE&amp;K</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoar_Construction" title="Hoar Construction">Hoar Construction</a>, and <a href="/wiki/B.L._Harbert_International" title="B.L. Harbert International">B.L. Harbert International</a>, based in Alabama and subsidiaries of <a href="/wiki/URS_Corporation" title="URS Corporation">URS Corporation</a>, are all routinely are included in the Engineering News-Record lists of top design, international construction, and engineering firms.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Law_and_government">Law and government</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="State_government">State government</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Alabama" title="Government of Alabama">Government of Alabama</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg/220px-Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg/330px-Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg/440px-Alabama_Capitol_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="595" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Capitol" title="Alabama State Capitol">State Capitol Building</a> in Montgomery, completed in 1851</figcaption></figure>
<p>The foundational document for Alabama's government is the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Alabama" title="Constitution of Alabama">Alabama Constitution</a>, the current one having been adopted in 2022.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2023)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Alabama <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Constitution_of_1901" title="Alabama Constitution of 1901">constitution adopted in 1901</a> was, with over 850 amendments and almost 87,000 words, by some accounts the world's longest constitution and roughly forty times the length of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post-222">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-223">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There has been a significant movement to rewrite and modernize Alabama's constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Critics have argued that Alabama's constitution maintains highly centralized power with the state legislature, leaving practically no power in local hands. Most counties do not have home rule. Any policy changes proposed in different areas of the state must be approved by the entire Alabama legislature and, frequently, by state referendum. The former constitution was particularly criticized for its complexity and length intentionally codifying segregation and racism.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg/220px-Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg/330px-Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg/440px-Ala_Supreme_Court_Building_Feb_2012_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Judicial_Building" title="Alabama Judicial Building">Heflin-Torbert Judicial Building</a> in Montgomery. It houses the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Alabama" title="Supreme Court of Alabama">Supreme Court of Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Court_of_Civil_Appeals" title="Alabama Court of Civil Appeals">Alabama Court of Civil Appeals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Court_of_Criminal_Appeals" title="Alabama Court of Criminal Appeals">Alabama Court of Criminal Appeals</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Alabama's government is divided into three coequal branches. The <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative branch</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Legislature" title="Alabama Legislature">Alabama Legislature</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> assembly composed of the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_House_of_Representatives" title="Alabama House of Representatives">Alabama House of Representatives</a>, with 105 members, and the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Senate" title="Alabama Senate">Alabama Senate</a>, with 35 members. The Legislature is responsible for writing, debating, passing, or defeating state legislation. The <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> currently holds a majority in both houses of the Legislature. The Legislature has the power to override a gubernatorial veto by a simple majority (most state Legislatures require a two-thirds majority to override a veto).
</p><p>Until 1964, the state elected state senators on a geographic basis by county, with one per county. It had not redistricted congressional districts since passage of its constitution in 1901; as a result, urbanized areas were grossly underrepresented. It had not changed legislative districts to reflect the decennial censuses, either. In <i>Reynolds v. Sims</i> (1964), the U.S. Supreme Court implemented the principle of "one man, one vote", ruling that congressional districts had to be reapportioned based on censuses (as the state already included in its constitution but had not implemented.) Further, the court ruled that both houses of bicameral state legislatures had to be apportioned by population, as there was no constitutional basis for states to have geographically based systems.
</p><p>At that time, Alabama and many other states had to change their legislative districting, as many across the country had systems that underrepresented urban areas and districts. This had caused decades of underinvestment in such areas. For instance, Birmingham and Jefferson County taxes had supplied one-third of the state budget, but Jefferson County received only 1/67th of state services in funding. Through the legislative delegations, the Alabama legislature kept control of county governments.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="300" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Governor_Kay_Ivey_2017_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="783" data-file-height="1069" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Kay_Ivey" title="Kay Ivey">Kay Ivey</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor of Alabama">governor of Alabama</a> as of 2024.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive branch</a> is responsible for the execution and oversight of laws. It is headed by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Alabama" title="List of governors of Alabama">governor of Alabama</a>. Other members of the executive branch include the cabinet, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_lieutenant_governors_of_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="List of lieutenant governors of Alabama">lieutenant governor of Alabama</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Alabama" title="Attorney General of Alabama">Attorney General of Alabama</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Alabama" title="Secretary of State of Alabama">Alabama Secretary of State</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Treasurer" title="Alabama State Treasurer">Alabama State Treasurer</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/State_Auditor_of_Alabama" title="State Auditor of Alabama">State Auditor of Alabama</a>. The current governor is Republican <a href="/wiki/Kay_Ivey" title="Kay Ivey">Kay Ivey</a>.
</p><p>The members of the Legislature take office immediately after the November elections. Statewide officials, such as the governor, lieutenant governor, attorney general, and other constitutional officers, take office the following January.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is responsible for interpreting the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Alabama" title="Constitution of Alabama">Constitution of Alabama</a> and applying the law in state criminal and civil cases. The <a href="/wiki/State_supreme_court" title="State supreme court">state's highest court</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Alabama" title="Supreme Court of Alabama">Supreme Court of Alabama</a>. Alabama uses partisan elections to select judges. Since the 1980s judicial campaigns have become increasingly politicized.<sup id="cite_ref-AJS_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJS-226">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The current <a href="/wiki/Chief_justice" title="Chief justice">chief justice</a> of the Alabama Supreme Court is Republican <a href="/wiki/Tom_Parker_(judge)" title="Tom Parker (judge)">Tom Parker</a>. All sitting justices on the Alabama Supreme Court are members of the Republican Party. There are two intermediate <a href="/wiki/Appellate_court" title="Appellate court">appellate courts</a>, the Court of Civil Appeals and the Court of Criminal Appeals, and four <a href="/wiki/Trial_court" title="Trial court">trial courts</a>: the circuit court (trial court of general jurisdiction), and the district, probate, and municipal courts.<sup id="cite_ref-AJS_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJS-226">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama has the death penalty with authorized methods of execution that include the <a href="/wiki/Electric_chair" title="Electric chair">electric chair</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gas_chamber" title="Gas chamber">gas chamber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Some critics believe the election of judges has contributed to an exceedingly high rate of executions.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Alabama has the highest per capita <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Alabama" title="Capital punishment in Alabama">death penalty rate</a> in the country. In some years, it imposes more death sentences than does Texas, a state which has a population five times larger.<sup id="cite_ref-npr.org_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-229">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> However, executions per capita are significantly higher in Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Some of its cases have been highly controversial; the U.S. Supreme Court has overturned<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> 24 convictions in death penalty cases.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It was the only state to allow judges to override jury decisions in whether or not to use a death sentence; in 10 cases judges overturned sentences of <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment" title="Life imprisonment">life imprisonment without parole</a> that were voted unanimously by juries.<sup id="cite_ref-npr.org_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-229">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> This judicial authority was removed in April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 14, 2019, Alabama passed the <a href="/wiki/Human_Life_Protection_Act" title="Human Life Protection Act">Human Life Protection Act</a>, banning abortion at any stage of pregnancy unless there is a "serious health risk", with no exceptions for rape and <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a>. The law subjects doctors who perform abortions with 10 to 99 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The law was originally supposed to take effect the following November, but on October 29, 2019, U.S. District Judge <a href="/wiki/Myron_H._Thompson" title="Myron H. Thompson">Myron Thompson</a> blocked the law from taking effect due to it being in conflict with the 1973 <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a> case <i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> On June 24, 2022, after the U.S. Supreme Court overturned <i>Roe v. Wade</i> in <i><a href="/wiki/Dobbs_v._Jackson_Women%27s_Health_Organization" title="Dobbs v. Jackson Women&#39;s Health Organization">Dobbs v. Jackson Women's Health Organization</a></i>, Judge Thompson lifted the injunction, allowing the law to go into effect.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama is one of the very few states that does not allow the creation of state lotteries.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Taxes">Taxes</h3></div>
<p>Taxes are collected by the Alabama Department of Revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Alabama levies a 2%, 4%, or<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>5% <a href="/wiki/State_income_tax" title="State income tax">personal income tax</a>, depending on the amount earned and filing status.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Taxpayers are allowed to deduct their <a href="/wiki/Income_tax_in_the_United_States" title="Income tax in the United States">federal income tax</a> from their Alabama state tax, even if taking the <a href="/wiki/Standard_deduction" title="Standard deduction">standard deduction</a>; those who itemize can also deduct <a href="/wiki/Federal_Insurance_Contributions_Act_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Insurance Contributions Act tax">FICA</a> (the Social Security and Medicare tax).<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The state's general sales tax rate is 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Sales tax rates for cities and counties are also added to purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> For example, the total sales tax rate in <a href="/wiki/Mobile_County,_Alabama" title="Mobile County, Alabama">Mobile County, Alabama</a> is 10% and there is an additional restaurant tax of 1%, which means a diner in <a href="/wiki/Mobile_County,_Alabama" title="Mobile County, Alabama">Mobile County, Alabama</a> would pay an 11% tax on a meal.
</p><p>In 2020, sales and excise taxes in Alabama accounted for 38% of all state and local revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Only Alabama, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> tax groceries at the full state sales tax rate.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The corporate income tax rate in Alabama is 6.5%. The overall federal, state, and local tax burden in Alabama ranks the state as the second least tax-burdened state in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">Property taxes</a> of .40% of assessed value per year, are the second-lowest in the U.S., after Hawaii.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> The state constitution currently requires a voter referendum to raise property taxes.
</p>

href="/wiki/Houston_County,_Alabama" shape="poly" coords="244,306,221,306,221,309,218,309,216,312,207,309,202,316,217,316,217,331,251,331" alt="Houston County, Alabama" title="Houston County, Alabama" /></map><figcaption>Alabama counties (clickable map)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Alabama has 67 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>. Each county has its own elected legislative branch, usually called the county commission. It also has limited executive authority in the county. Because of the constraints of the Alabama Constitution, which centralizes power in the state legislature, only seven counties (Jefferson, Lee, Mobile, Madison, Montgomery, Shelby, and Tuscaloosa) in the state have limited <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a>. Instead, most counties in the state must lobby the Local Legislation Committee of the state legislature to get simple local policies approved, ranging from waste disposal to land use zoning.
</p><p>The state legislature has retained power over local governments by refusing to pass a constitutional amendment establishing home rule for counties, as recommended by the 1973 Alabama Constitutional Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-home_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-home-246">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Legislative delegations retain certain powers over each county. United States Supreme Court decisions in <i>Baker v. Carr</i> (1964) required that both houses have districts established on the basis of population, and redistricted after each census, to implement the principle of "one man, one vote". Before that, each county was represented by one state senator, leading to under-representation in the state senate for more urbanized, populous counties. The rural bias of the state legislature, which had also failed to redistrict seats in the state house, affected politics well into the 20th century, failing to recognize the rise of industrial cities and urbanized areas.
</p><p>"The lack of home rule for counties in Alabama has resulted in the proliferation of local legislation permitting counties to do things not authorized by the state constitution. Alabama's constitution has been amended more than 700 times, and almost one-third of the amendments are local in nature, applying to only one county or city. A significant part of each legislative session is spent on local legislation, taking away time and attention of legislators from issues of statewide importance."<sup id="cite_ref-home_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-home-246">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alabama is an <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage_control_state" title="Alcoholic beverage control state">alcoholic beverage control state</a>, meaning the state government holds a monopoly on the sale of alcohol. The <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Alcoholic_Beverage_Control_Board" title="Alabama Alcoholic Beverage Control Board">Alabama Alcoholic Beverage Control Board</a> controls the sale and distribution of alcoholic beverages in the state. A total of 25 of the 67 counties are "<a href="/wiki/Dry_county" title="Dry county">dry counties</a>" which ban the sale of alcohol, and there are many dry municipalities in counties which permit alcohol sales.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Politics">Politics</h3></div>
<p>During Reconstruction following the American Civil War, Alabama was occupied by federal troops of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Military_District" title="Third Military District">Third Military District</a> under <a href="/wiki/John_Pope_(military_officer)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Pope (military officer)">General John Pope</a>. In 1874, the political coalition of white Democrats known as the <a href="/wiki/Redeemers" title="Redeemers">Redeemers</a> took control of the state government from the Republicans, in part by suppressing the black vote through violence, fraud, and intimidation. After 1890, a coalition of White Democratic politicians passed laws to segregate and disenfranchise African American residents, a process completed in provisions of the 1901 constitution. Provisions which disenfranchised blacks resulted in excluding many poor Whites. By 1941 more Whites than Blacks had been disenfranchised: 600,000 to 520,000. The total effects were greater on the black community, as almost all its citizens were disfranchised and relegated to separate and unequal treatment under the law.
</p><p>From 1901 through the 1960s, the state did not redraw election districts as population grew and shifted within the state during urbanization and industrialization of certain areas. As counties were the basis of election districts, the result was a rural minority that dominated state politics through nearly three-quarters of the century, until a series of federal court cases required redistricting in 1972 to meet equal representation. Alabama state politics gained nationwide and international attention in the 1950s and 1960s during the civil rights movement, when whites bureaucratically, and at times violently, resisted protests for electoral and social reform. Governor George Wallace, the state's only four-term governor, was a controversial figure who vowed to maintain segregation. Only after passage of the federal Civil Rights Act of 1964<sup id="cite_ref-cra64_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cra64-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and Voting Rights Act of 1965 did African Americans regain the ability to exercise suffrage, among other civil rights. In many jurisdictions, they continued to be excluded from representation by at-large electoral systems, which allowed the majority of the population to dominate elections. Some changes at the county level have occurred following court challenges to establish <a href="/wiki/Single-member_district" title="Single-member district">single-member districts</a> that enable a more diverse representation among county boards.
</p><p>In 2007, the Alabama Legislature passed, and Republican governor <a href="/wiki/Bob_Riley" title="Bob Riley">Bob Riley</a> signed a resolution expressing "profound regret" over slavery and its lingering impact. In a symbolic ceremony, the bill was signed in the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Capitol" title="Alabama State Capitol">Alabama State Capitol</a>, which housed Congress of the Confederate States of America.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Republicans won control of both houses of the legislature for the first time in 136 years.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of February&#160;2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alabama&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there are a total of 3,707,233 registered voters, with 3,318,679 active, and the others inactive in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2023 <i>American Values Atlas</i> by <a href="/wiki/Public_Religion_Research_Institute" title="Public Religion Research Institute">Public Religion Research Institute</a> found that a majority of Alabama residents support <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Elections">Elections</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Alabama" title="Elections in Alabama">Elections in Alabama</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg/220px-Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg/330px-Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg/440px-Doug_Jones_Biden_Event.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a><figcaption>Senator <a href="/wiki/Doug_Jones_(politician)" title="Doug Jones (politician)">Doug Jones</a> won a <a href="/wiki/2017_United_States_Senate_special_election_in_Alabama" title="2017 United States Senate special election in Alabama">special election</a> in 2017.</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="State_elections">State elections</h4></div>
<p>With the disfranchisement of Blacks in 1901, the state became part of the "<a href="/wiki/Solid_South" title="Solid South">Solid South</a>", a system in which the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> operated as effectively the only viable political party in every Southern state. For nearly a hundred years local and state elections in Alabama were decided in the Democratic Party <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">primary</a>, with generally only token <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> challengers running in the general election. Since the mid- to late 20th century, however, white conservatives started shifting to the Republican Party. In Alabama, majority-white districts are now expected to regularly elect Republican candidates to federal, state and local office.
</p><p>Members of the nine seats on the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Alabama" title="Supreme Court of Alabama">Supreme Court of Alabama</a><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> and all ten seats on the state appellate courts are elected to office. Until 1994, no Republicans held any of the court seats. In that general election, the then-incumbent chief justice, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_C._Hornsby" title="Ernest C. Hornsby">Ernest C. Hornsby</a>, refused to leave office after losing the election by approximately 3,000 votes to Republican <a href="/wiki/Perry_Hooper_Sr." title="Perry Hooper Sr.">Perry O. Hooper Sr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Hornsby sued Alabama and defiantly remained in office for nearly a year before finally giving up the seat after losing in court.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> The Democrats lost the last of the nineteen court seats in August 2011 with the resignation of the last Democrat on the bench.
</p><p>In the early 21st century, Republicans hold all seven of the statewide elected executive branch offices. Republicans hold six of the eight elected seats on the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Board_of_Education" title="Alabama State Board of Education">Alabama State Board of Education</a>. In 2010, Republicans took large majorities of both chambers of the state legislature, giving them control of that body for the first time in 136 years. The last remaining statewide Democrat, who served on the Alabama Public Service Commission, was defeated in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Only three Republican lieutenant governors have been elected since the end of Reconstruction, when Republicans generally represented Reconstruction government, including the newly emancipated freedmen who had gained the franchise. The three GOP lieutenant governors are <a href="/wiki/Steve_Windom" title="Steve Windom">Steve Windom</a> (1999–2003), <a href="/wiki/Kay_Ivey" title="Kay Ivey">Kay Ivey</a> (2011–2017), and <a href="/wiki/Will_Ainsworth" title="Will Ainsworth">Will Ainsworth</a> (2019–present).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Local_elections">Local elections</h4></div>
<p>Many local offices (county commissioners, boards of education, tax assessors, mayors, etc.) in the state are still held by Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> Many metropolitan and suburban counties have voters who are majority Democrats, resulting in local elections being decided in the Democratic primary. Similarly most rural counties are majority-Republican and elections are effectively decided in the Republican Primary. However, since local governments in Alabama are weaker than in other parts of the country, Republicans have the upper hand in government.
</p><p>Alabama's 67 county sheriffs are elected in partisan, at-large races, and Republicans retain the vast majority of those posts. The current split is 18 <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Democratic_Party" title="Alabama Democratic Party">Democrats</a>, and 49 <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Republican_Party" title="Alabama Republican Party">Republicans</a> as of 2023. However, most of the Democratic sheriffs preside over urban and more populated counties. The majority of Republican sheriffs have been elected in the more rural counties with lower population. The state of Alabama has and 11 African-American sheriffs.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Federal_elections">Federal elections</h4></div>
<p>The state's two <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. senators</a> are <a href="/wiki/Katie_Britt" title="Katie Britt">Katie Britt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Tuberville" title="Tommy Tuberville">Tommy Tuberville</a>, both of whom are Republican. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a>, the state is represented by seven members, six of whom are Republicans: (<a href="/wiki/Jerry_Carl" title="Jerry Carl">Jerry Carl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rogers_(Alabama_politician)" title="Mike Rogers (Alabama politician)">Mike Rogers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Aderholt" title="Robert Aderholt">Robert Aderholt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dale_Strong" title="Dale Strong">Dale Strong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Moore_(Alabama_politician)" title="Barry Moore (Alabama politician)">Barry Moore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Palmer_(politician)" title="Gary Palmer (politician)">Gary Palmer</a>) and one Democrat: <a href="/wiki/Terri_Sewell" title="Terri Sewell">Terri Sewell</a>, who represents the Black Belt as well as most of the predominantly black portions of Birmingham, Tuscaloosa and Montgomery.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Alabama" title="Education in Alabama">Education in Alabama</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg/220px-Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg/330px-Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg/440px-Vestavia_Hills_High_School.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="539" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Vestavia_Hills_High_School" title="Vestavia Hills High School">Vestavia Hills High School</a> in the suburbs of Birmingham</figcaption></figure>
<p>Public primary and secondary education in Alabama is under the purview of the Alabama State Board of Education as well as local oversight by 67 county school boards and 60 city boards of education. Together, 1,496 individual schools provide education for 744,637 elementary and secondary students.<sup id="cite_ref-qfacts_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qfacts-261">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Public school funding is appropriated through the Alabama Legislature through the Education Trust Fund. In FY 2006–2007, Alabama appropriated $3,775,163,578 for primary and secondary education. That represented an increase of $444,736,387 over the previous fiscal year. In 2007, more than 82 percent of schools made adequate yearly progress (AYP) toward student proficiency under the National <a href="/wiki/No_Child_Left_Behind_Act" title="No Child Left Behind Act">No Child Left Behind</a> law, using measures determined by the state of Alabama.
</p><p>While Alabama's public education system has improved in recent decades, it lags behind in achievement compared to other states. According to U.S. Census data (2000), Alabama's high school graduation rate (75%) is the fourth lowest in the U.S. (after <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and Mississippi).<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> The largest educational gains were among people with some college education but without degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> According to National Assessment of Educational Progress (NEAP), Alabama ranks 39 in reading and 40 in math among fourth-grade students in the rankings from 2022.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.nationsreportcard.gov/profiles/stateprofile/overview/NP?cti=PgTab_ScoreComparisons&amp;chort=1&amp;sub=RED&amp;sj=NP&amp;fs=SubjectLabel&amp;st=MN&amp;year=2022R3&amp;sg=Gender%3A%20Male%20vs.%20Female&amp;sgv=Difference&amp;ts=Single%20Year&amp;tss=-2022R3&amp;sfj=NP">[1]</a>
</p><p>Generally prohibited in the West at large, <a href="/wiki/School_corporal_punishment" title="School corporal punishment">school corporal punishment</a> is not unusual in Alabama, with 27,260 public school students <a href="/wiki/Paddle_(spanking)" title="Paddle (spanking)">paddled</a> at least one time, according to government data for the 2011–2012 school year.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CORPUN_US_SCHOOL_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CORPUN_US_SCHOOL-265">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The rate of school corporal punishment in Alabama is surpassed by only Mississippi and Arkansas.<sup id="cite_ref-CORPUN_US_SCHOOL_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CORPUN_US_SCHOOL-265">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Alabama" title="List of colleges and universities in Alabama">List of colleges and universities in Alabama</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison-plaza2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Harrison-plaza2.jpg/220px-Harrison-plaza2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Harrison-plaza2.jpg/330px-Harrison-plaza2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Harrison-plaza2.jpg/440px-Harrison-plaza2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>Harrison Plaza at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Alabama" title="University of North Alabama">University of North Alabama</a> in Florence. The school was chartered as LaGrange College by the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Legislature" title="Alabama Legislature">Alabama Legislature</a> in 1830.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Alabama's programs of higher education include 14 four-year public universities, two-year community colleges, and 17 private, undergraduate and graduate universities. In the state are four medical schools (as of fall 2015) <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_at_Birmingham_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Alabama at Birmingham School of Medicine">UAB Heersink School of Medicine</a>, University of South Alabama and <a href="/wiki/Alabama_College_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Alabama College of Osteopathic Medicine">Alabama College of Osteopathic Medicine</a> and The Edward Via College of Osteopathic Medicine—Auburn Campus), two veterinary colleges (Auburn University and <a href="/wiki/Tuskegee_University" title="Tuskegee University">Tuskegee University</a>), a dental school (<a href="/wiki/UAB_School_of_Dentistry" title="UAB School of Dentistry">UAB School of Dentistry</a>, an optometry college (UAB School of Optometry), two pharmacy schools (Auburn University and <a href="/wiki/Samford_University" title="Samford University">Samford University</a>), and five law schools (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_School_of_Law" title="University of Alabama School of Law">University of Alabama School of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_School_of_Law" title="Birmingham School of Law">Birmingham School of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_School_of_Law" title="Cumberland School of Law">Cumberland School of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miles_Law_School" title="Miles Law School">Miles Law School</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Goode_Jones_School_of_Law" title="Thomas Goode Jones School of Law">Thomas Goode Jones School of Law</a>). Public, post-secondary education in Alabama is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Commission_on_Higher_Education" title="Alabama Commission on Higher Education">Alabama Commission on Higher Education</a> and the Alabama Department of Postsecondary Education. Colleges and universities in Alabama offer degree programs from two-year associate degrees to a multitude of doctoral level programs.<sup id="cite_ref-ache_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ache-266">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg/220px-William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg/330px-William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg/440px-William_J._Samford_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1111" /></a><figcaption>William J. Samford Hall at <a href="/wiki/Auburn_University" title="Auburn University">Auburn University</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The largest single campus is the University of Alabama, located in Tuscaloosa, with 37,665 enrolled for fall 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Troy University was the largest institution in the state in 2010, with an enrollment of 29,689 students across four Alabama campuses (<a href="/wiki/Troy,_Alabama" title="Troy, Alabama">Troy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dothan,_Alabama" title="Dothan, Alabama">Dothan</a>, Montgomery, and <a href="/wiki/Phenix_City,_Alabama" title="Phenix City, Alabama">Phenix City</a>), as well as sixty learning sites in seventeen other states and eleven other countries. The oldest institutions are the public <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Alabama" title="University of North Alabama">University of North Alabama</a> in Florence and the Catholic Church-affiliated <a href="/wiki/Spring_Hill_College" title="Spring Hill College">Spring Hill College</a> in Mobile, both founded in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-una_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-una-268">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shc_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shc-269">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Accreditation of academic programs is through the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Southern Association of Colleges and Schools">Southern Association of Colleges and Schools</a> (SACS) as well as other subject-focused national and international accreditation agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Biblical_Higher_Education" title="Association for Biblical Higher Education">Association for Biblical Higher Education</a> (ABHE),<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Council_on_Occupational_Education" title="Council on Occupational Education">Council on Occupational Education</a> (COE),<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Accrediting_Council_for_Independent_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Accrediting Council for Independent Colleges and Schools">Accrediting Council for Independent Colleges and Schools</a> (ACICS).<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2024 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>, Alabama had three universities ranked in the top 100 Public Schools in America (<a href="/wiki/Auburn_University" title="Auburn University">Auburn University</a> at 47, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_at_Birmingham" title="University of Alabama at Birmingham">University of Alabama at Birmingham</a> (UAB) at 76, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama" title="University of Alabama">University of Alabama</a> at 91).<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2024 <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>, Alabama had four <a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">tier one</a> universities (Auburn University, University of Alabama at Birmingham (UAB), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama" title="University of Alabama">University of Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_in_Huntsville" title="University of Alabama in Huntsville">University of Alabama in Huntsville</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Media">Media</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Mass_media_in_Alabama" title="Category:Mass media in Alabama">Category:Mass media in Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Alabama" title="List of newspapers in Alabama">List of newspapers in Alabama</a></div>
<p>Major newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Birmingham_News" title="The Birmingham News">Birmingham News</a></i>, Mobile <i><a href="/wiki/Press-Register" title="Press-Register">Press-Register</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Advertiser" title="Montgomery Advertiser">Montgomery Advertiser</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Major television network affiliates in Alabama include:
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2></div>

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></span></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alabama&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Literature">Literature</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alabama_literature" title="Alabama literature">Alabama literature</a></div>
<p>Alabama literature is characterized by themes of race and issues of gender and war, and is influenced by events such as the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">Reconstruction era</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Rights Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. Some notable examples of Alabama literature include Harper Lee's <i><a href="/wiki/To_Kill_A_Mockingbird" class="mw-redirect" title="To Kill A Mockingbird">To Kill A Mockingbird</a></i>, Winston Groom's <i><a href="/wiki/Forrest_Gump_(novel)" title="Forrest Gump (novel)">Forrest Gump</a></i>, Fannie Flagg's <i><a href="/wiki/Fried_Green_Tomatoes_at_the_Whistlestop_Cafe" class="mw-redirect" title="Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistlestop Cafe">Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistlestop Cafe</a></i>, and the biographies of <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Parks" title="Rosa Parks">Rosa Parks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium,_Tuscaloosa_AL,_North_view_20160714_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium%2C_Tuscaloosa_AL%2C_North_view_20160714_1.jpg/220px-Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium%2C_Tuscaloosa_AL%2C_North_view_20160714_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium%2C_Tuscaloosa_AL%2C_North_view_20160714_1.jpg/330px-Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium%2C_Tuscaloosa_AL%2C_North_view_20160714_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium%2C_Tuscaloosa_AL%2C_North_view_20160714_1.jpg/440px-Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium%2C_Tuscaloosa_AL%2C_North_view_20160714_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6616" data-file-height="3888" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium" title="Bryant–Denny Stadium">Bryant–Denny Stadium</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama" title="University of Alabama">University of Alabama</a> in Tuscaloosa</figcaption></figure>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Professional_sports">Professional sports</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_professional_sports_teams_in_Alabama" title="List of professional sports teams in Alabama">List of professional sports teams in Alabama</a></div>
<p>Alabama has several professional and semi-professional sports teams, including three <a href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor league baseball">minor league baseball</a> teams.
</p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a> motorsports complex hosts a series of <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> events. It has a seating capacity of 143,000 and is the thirteenth largest stadium in the world and sixth largest stadium in America. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Barber_Motorsports_Park" title="Barber Motorsports Park">Barber Motorsports Park</a> has hosted <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rolex_Sports_Car_Series" title="Rolex Sports Car Series">Rolex Sports Car Series</a> races.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/ATP_Birmingham" title="ATP Birmingham">ATP Birmingham</a> was a <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Tennis" title="World Championship Tennis">World Championship Tennis</a> tournament held from 1973 to 1980.
</p><p>Alabama has hosted several professional golf tournaments, such as the 1984 and 1990 <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">PGA Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Shoal_Creek_Golf_and_Country_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Shoal Creek Golf and Country Club">Shoal Creek</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Barbasol_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbasol Championship">Barbasol Championship</a> (<a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_LPGA_Tournament_of_Champions" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile LPGA Tournament of Champions">Mobile LPGA Tournament of Champions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_LPGA_Classic" title="Airbus LPGA Classic">Airbus LPGA Classic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yokohama_Tire_LPGA_Classic" title="Yokohama Tire LPGA Classic">Yokohama Tire LPGA Classic</a> (<a href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="LPGA Tour">LPGA Tour</a>), and <a href="/wiki/The_Tradition" title="The Tradition">The Tradition</a> (<a href="/wiki/Champions_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Champions Tour">Champions Tour</a>).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="College_sports">College sports</h4></div>
<p>College football is extremely popular in Alabama, particularly the University of Alabama <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Crimson_Tide" title="Alabama Crimson Tide">Crimson Tide</a> and Auburn University <a href="/wiki/Auburn_Tigers" title="Auburn Tigers">Tigers</a>, rivals in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a>. Alabama averages over 100,000 fans per game and Auburn averages over 80,000—both numbers among the top twenty in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Bryant–Denny Stadium is the home of the Alabama football team, and has a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of 101,821,<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> and is the fifth largest stadium in America.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Jordan-Hare Stadium is the home field of the Auburn football team and seats up to 87,451.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Protective_Stadium" title="Protective Stadium">Protective Stadium</a> is home of the <a href="/wiki/UAB_Blazers" title="UAB Blazers">UAB Blazers</a> football program and the <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Bowl" title="Birmingham Bowl">Birmingham Bowl</a>. It seats 45,000.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ladd%E2%80%93Peebles_Stadium" title="Ladd–Peebles Stadium">Ladd–Peebles Stadium</a> in Mobile is the home of the University of South Alabama football team, and serves as the home of the NCAA <a href="/wiki/Senior_Bowl" title="Senior Bowl">Senior Bowl</a>, <a href="/wiki/LendingTree_Bowl" class="mw-redirect" title="LendingTree Bowl">LendingTree Bowl</a>, and Alabama-Mississippi All Star Classic; the stadium seats 40,646.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Bryant–Denny Stadium and Jordan-Hare Stadium became the homes of the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_High_School_Athletic_Association" title="Alabama High School Athletic Association">Alabama High School Athletic Association</a> state football championship games, after previously being held at Legion Field in Birmingham.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Alabama" title="Transportation in Alabama">Transportation in Alabama</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG/220px-Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG/330px-Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG/440px-Montgomery_Regional_Airport_New_Terminal.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>Terminal at the <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Regional_Airport" title="Montgomery Regional Airport">Montgomery Regional Airport</a> in Montgomery</figcaption></figure>
