<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Aviation">Aviation</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_Alabama" title="Aviation in Alabama">Aviation in Alabama</a></div>
<p>Major airports with sustained operations in Alabama include <a href="/wiki/Birmingham-Shuttlesworth_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Birmingham-Shuttlesworth International Airport">Birmingham-Shuttlesworth International Airport</a> (BHM), <a href="/wiki/Huntsville_International_Airport" title="Huntsville International Airport">Huntsville International Airport</a> (HSV), <a href="/wiki/Dothan_Regional_Airport" title="Dothan Regional Airport">Dothan Regional Airport</a> (DHN), <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Regional_Airport" title="Mobile Regional Airport">Mobile Regional Airport</a> (MOB), <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Regional_Airport" title="Montgomery Regional Airport">Montgomery Regional Airport</a> (MGM), <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Alabama_Regional_Airport" title="Northwest Alabama Regional Airport">Northwest Alabama Regional Airport</a> (MSL) and <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Alabama_Regional_Airport" title="Northeast Alabama Regional Airport">Northeast Alabama Regional Airport</a> (GAD).
</p>

<p>For rail transport, <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> schedules the <i><a href="/wiki/Crescent_(train)" title="Crescent (train)">Crescent</a></i>, a daily passenger train, running from New York to New Orleans with station stops at <a href="/wiki/Anniston_station" title="Anniston station">Anniston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_station_(Alabama)" title="Birmingham station (Alabama)">Birmingham</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuscaloosa_station" title="Tuscaloosa station">Tuscaloosa</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Roads">Roads</h3></div>
<p>Alabama has six major interstate routes: <a href="/wiki/Interstate_65_in_Alabama" title="Interstate 65 in Alabama">Interstate 65</a> (I-65) travels north–south roughly through the middle of the state; <a href="/wiki/Interstate_20_in_Alabama" title="Interstate 20 in Alabama">I-20</a>/<a href="/wiki/Interstate_59_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 59 in Alabama">I-59</a> travel from the central west Mississippi state line to Birmingham, where I-59 continues to the north-east corner of the state and I-20 continues east towards <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>; <a href="/wiki/Interstate_85_in_Alabama" title="Interstate 85 in Alabama">I-85</a> originates in Montgomery and travels east-northeast to the Georgia state line, providing a main thoroughfare to Atlanta; and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10_in_Alabama" title="Interstate 10 in Alabama">I-10</a> traverses the southernmost portion of the state, traveling from west to east through Mobile. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_22_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 22 in Alabama">I-22</a> enters the state from Mississippi and connects Birmingham with <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis, Tennessee</a>. In addition, there are currently five auxiliary interstate routes in the state: <a href="/wiki/Interstate_165_(Alabama)" title="Interstate 165 (Alabama)">I-165</a> in Mobile, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_359" title="Interstate 359">I-359</a> in Tuscaloosa, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_459" title="Interstate 459">I-459</a> around Birmingham, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_565" title="Interstate 565">I-565</a> in Decatur and Huntsville, and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_759" title="Interstate 759">I-759</a> in Gadsden. A sixth route, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_685_(Alabama)" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 685 (Alabama)">I-685</a>, will be formed when I-85 is rerouted along a new southern bypass of Montgomery. A proposed northern bypass of Birmingham will be designated as <a href="/wiki/Interstate_422" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 422">I-422</a>. Since a direct connection from I-22 to I-422 will not be possible, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_222" class="mw-redirect" title="Interstate 222">I-222</a> has been proposed, as well.
</p><p>Several U.S. Highways also pass through the state, such as <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_11_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 11 in Alabama">U.S. Route 11</a> (US-11), <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_29_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 29 in Alabama">US-29</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_31_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 31 in Alabama">US-31</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_43_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 43 in Alabama">US-43</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_45_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 45 in Alabama">US-45</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_72_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 72 in Alabama">US-72</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_78_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 78 in Alabama">US-78</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_80_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 80 in Alabama">US-80</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_82_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 82 in Alabama">US-82</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_84_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 84 in Alabama">US-84</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_90_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 90 in Alabama">US-90</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_98_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 98 in Alabama">US-98</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_231_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 231 in Alabama">US-231</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_278_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 278 in Alabama">US-278</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_280_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 280 in Alabama">US-280</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_331_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 331 in Alabama">US-331</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_411_in_Alabama" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 411 in Alabama">US-411</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_431_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 431 in Alabama">US-431</a>.
</p><p>There are four toll roads in the state: Montgomery Expressway in Montgomery; Northport/Tuscaloosa Western Bypass in Tuscaloosa and <a href="/wiki/Northport,_Alabama" title="Northport, Alabama">Northport</a>; Emerald Mountain Expressway in Wetumpka; and Beach Express in <a href="/wiki/Orange_Beach,_Alabama" title="Orange Beach, Alabama">Orange Beach</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ports">Ports</h3></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Mobile" title="Port of Mobile">Port of Mobile</a>, Alabama's only saltwater port, is a large seaport on the Gulf of Mexico with inland waterway access to the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a> by way of the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee%E2%80%93Tombigbee_Waterway" title="Tennessee–Tombigbee Waterway">Tennessee–Tombigbee Waterway</a>. The Port of Mobile was ranked 12th by tons of traffic in the United States during 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-tonstraffic_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tonstraffic-284">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> The newly expanded <a href="/wiki/Container_port" title="Container port">container terminal</a> at the Port of Mobile was ranked as the 25th busiest for container traffic in the nation during 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-containers_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-containers-285">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> The state's other ports are on rivers with access to the Gulf of Mexico.
</p><p>Water ports of Alabama, listed from north to south:

<li>WPA <i>Guide to Alabama</i> (1939).</li></ul>
